Workshop
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) and the German Management Academy (DMAN) are jointly organizing the annual Campus on Public-Private Partnership for Development of Infrastructure and Social Services.
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) and the World Trade Organization (WTO) are jointly organizing a workshop on international trade negotiations, as part of their International Trade Series.
The workshop, to be conducted in English, will be held from Monday to Thursday, 10 to 13 December 2001, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m. and 3 p.m. to 6 p.m. at United Nations Headquarters.
A letter on this subject, including a detailed information note, the programme and a nomination form, was addressed to all Permanent Missions in New York.
The registration deadline is Wednesday, 5 December.
For further information, please contact Ms. Cecelia Coleman at UNITAR (room DC1-603, tel.: 963-9684 and 963-9196).
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) is conducting a workshop on team development.
This workshop, to be conducted in English, will be held on Tuesday, 18 December 2001, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m. and from 3 p.m. to 6 p.m., and on Wednesday, 19 December, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m.
A letter on this subject, including a detailed information note, an outline of activities and a nomination form, was addressed to all Permanent Missions in New York.
Members from United Nations agencies are also encouraged to apply.
The registration deadline is Tuesday, 11 December.
For further information, please contact Ms. Cecelia Coleman at UNITAR (room DC1-603; tel.: (212) 963-9684 and 963-9196).
As from Thursday, 1 November 2001, and for the rest of the month, the President of the Security Council will conduct informal briefings daily on the current work of the Council for Member States of the United Nations which are non-members of the Council, except on days on which no informal consultations are scheduled.
The briefings will take place immediately following the adjournment of the informal consultations in the Press Briefing Room (S-226).
A Web site of the Presidency of the Security Council has been established with effect on Thursday, 1 November 2001 and can be visited at the following address: http://www.un.org/Docs/sc/presidency.
The Web site of the President of the General Assembly can be visited at the following address: http://www. un.org/ga/president.
The President's statements and a summary of his daily activities are available on this Web site.

SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Thursday, 29 November 2001
4431st meeting
The situation between Iraq and Kuwait
Report of the Secretary-General pursuant to paragraph 5 of resolution 1360 (2001) (S/2001/1089)
The agenda was adopted without objection.
The President drew attention to the text of a draft resolution contained in document S/2001/1123, which had been prepared in the course of the Council's prior consultations, and made an oral revision to the text in its provisional form.
The Council then proceeded to the voste on the draft resolution (S/2001/1123) before it, as orally revised in its provisional form.
Decision: The draft resolution (S/2001/1123), as orally revised in its provisional form, received 15 votes in favour, none against and no abstentions, and was adopted unanimously as resolution 1382 (2001).

Advancement of women [112]
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.21/Rev.1
The Committee was informed that the draft resolution contained no programme budget implications.
The representative of Suriname orally revised the revised draft resolution and announced that Belgium, Germany, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, Portugal, Saint Kitts and Nevis, Spain and Trinidad and Tobago had joined in sponsoring the revised draft resolution.
Afghanistan, Bangladesh, Bolivia, Burkina Faso, Chile, Colombia, Croatia, Cyprus, Fiji, Greece, Guatemala, Guinea, Honduras, Ireland, Italy, Panama, the Philippines and Uganda joined in sponsoring the revised draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the revised draft resolution, as orally revised, without a vote.

Angola joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Draft decision

The Committee thus concluded its consideration of agenda item 114.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.40
The representative of Suriname orally revised the draft resolution and announced that Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Benin, Cameroon, Costa Rica, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, Dominica, Grenada, Kenya, Saint Kitts and Nevis and Saint Lucia joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Subsequently, Bangladesh, Burkina Faso, Fiji, Namibia, the Netherlands, Sierra Leone and Togo joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Before the adoption of the draft resolution, a statement was made by the representative of Haiti.
The representative of the United States made an oral correction to the text.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, as orally revised and corrected, without a vote.
After the adoption of the draft resolution, statements were made by the representatives of Egypt and Suriname.

The Committee was informed that the revised draft resolution contained no programme budget implications.

The Committee adopted the revised draft resolution, without a vote.

A message was received from UNESCO.

World AIDS Day
World AIDS Day will be observed today, 30 November 2001, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in Conference Room 4.
A townhall meeting on the theme "I Care... Do You?", will also highlight 2001 as the International Year of Volunteers.
Mr. Shashi Tharoor, Interim Head of the Department of Public Information, will make welcoming remarks.
The President of the General Assembly, the Deputy Secretary-General and Desmond Johns, representative of UNAIDS Office in New York, will make opening remarks.
Participants will include Nane Annan; Thoraya Ahmed Obaid, Executive Director, UNFPA, and Chairperson, Committee of Co-sponsoring Agencies of UNAIDS; Eduardo Doryan, Special Representative to the United Nations, the World Bank Group; Noeleen Heyzer, Executive Director, UNIFEM; André Roberfroid, Deputy Executive Director, UNICEF; Eimi Watanabe, Assistant Administrator and Director, Bureau for Development Policy, UNDP; Wendy Fitzwilliam, Miss Universe 1998 and Goodwill Ambassador for HIV/AIDS; and Danny Glover, UNDP Goodwill Ambassador.
The moderator will be Daljit Dhaliwal, News Anchor, ITN, London.
The observance is co-sponsored by DPI, UNAIDS, UNICEF, UNDP, UNFPA, the ILO, WHO, the World Bank, UNIFEM and UNV.
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.
On the occasion of the International Day of Disabled Persons, an art exhibit entitled "United Colors", co-sponsored by the Division for Social Policy and Development, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be launched on Monday, 3 December 2001, at 6 p.m. at the south end of the lobby of the Secretariat Building.
Also in observance of the International Day, a panel discussion on "New Approaches to Assess Progress and Evaluate Outcomes", organized by the Division for Social Policy and Development, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be held on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 1.15 p.m. to 2.45 p.m. in Conference Room 9.
More information about the International Day will be available on the Internet at the following address: (http://www.un.org/esa/socdev/enable/disobs. htm).
Special tribute to Mr. Ismat T. Kittani
There will be special tribute to the memory of Mr. Ismat T. Kittani, former President of the General Assembly, United Nations Under-Secretary-General and senior Iraqi diplomat, on Tuesday, 4 December 2001, at 12 noon in the Economic and Social Council Chamber, with the participation of the Secretary-General.
All attending are kindly requested to be seated in the Chamber by 11.45 a.m.

SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Thursday, 29 November 2001
68th plenary meeting
Reports of the First Committee
The Rapporteur of the First Committee introduced the reports of the Committee on agenda items 64 to 84.
Reduction of military budgets: report of the First Committee (A/56/526) [64]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/526) (resolution 56/14).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 64.
Verification in all its aspects, including the role of the United Nations in the field of verification: report of the First Committee (A/56/527) [65]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/527) (resolution 56/15).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 65.
Implementation of the Declaration of the Indian Ocean as a Zone of Peace: report of the First Committee (A/56/528) [66]
By 110 votes to 3, with 41 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/528) (resolution 56/16).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 66.
African Nuclear-Weapon-Free Zone Treaty: report of the First Committee (A/56/529) [67]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 8 of its report (A/56/529) (resolution 56/17).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 67.
Maintenance of international security - good-neighbourliness, stability and development in South-Eastern Europe: report of the First Committee (A/56/530) [68]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/530) (resolution 56/18).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 68.
Developments in the field of information and telecommunications in the context of international security: report of the First Committee (A/56/533) [69]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 9 of its report (A/56/533) (resolution 56/19).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 69.
The role of science and technology in the context of international security and disarmament: report of the First Committee (A/56/531) [70]
By 92 votes to 46, with 17 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/531) (resolution 56/20).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 70.
Establishment of a nuclear-weapon-free zone in the region of the Middle East: report of the First Committee (A/56/532) [71]
The General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/532) (resolution 56/21).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 71.
Conclusion of effective international arrangements to assure non-nuclear-weapon States against the use or threat of use of nuclear weapons: report of the First Committee (A/56/534) [72]
By 105 votes to none, with 54 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/534) (resolution 56/22).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 72.
Prevention of an arms race in outer space: report of the First Committee (A/56/535) [73]
By 156 votes to none, with 4 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted the draft resolution recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 7 of its report (A/56/535) (resolution 56/23).
The Assembly decided to conclude its consideration of agenda item 73.
General and complete disarmament: report of the First Committee (A/56/536) [74]
The Assembly was informed that a decision on draft resolution U would be taken at a later date.
The Assembly proceeded to take decisions on draft resolutions A to T and V to W as well as draft decisions I to III recommended by the First Committee in paragraph 73 of its report (A/56/536).

of Disabled Persons
On the occasion of the International Day of Disabled Persons, an art exhibit entitled "United Colors", co-sponsored by the Division for Social Policy and Development, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be launched on Monday, 3 December 2001, at 6 p.m. at the south end of the lobby of the Secretariat Building.
Also in observance of the International Day, a panel discussion on "New Approaches to Assess Progress and Evaluate Outcomes", organized by the Division for Social Policy and Development, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be held on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 1.15 p.m. to 2.45 p.m. in Conference Room 9.

Special tribute to Mr. Ismat T. Kittani
There will be special tribute to the memory of Mr. Ismat T. Kittani, former President of the General Assembly, United Nations Under-Secretary-General and senior Iraqi diplomat, on Tuesday, 4 December 2001, at 12 noon in the Economic and Social Council Chamber, with the participation of the Secretary-General.
All attending are kindly requested to be seated in the Chamber by 11.45 a.m.
International Volunteer Day
On Wednesday, 5 December 2001, International Volunteer Day, a special event marking the closing of the International Year of Volunteers 2001 (IYV), to be presided over by the President of the General Assembly, will take place from 12 noon to 1 p.m. in the General Assembly Hall.
The event will be held in connection with the two plenary meetings of the General Assembly, which will be devoted to volunteering as decided by the General Assembly in its resolution 55/57.
Guest speakers will include His Royal Highness Prince of Asturias, D. Felipe de Borbon of Spain, and Dr. Nafis Sadik, former Executive Director of UNFPA, both appointed IYV Eminent Persons by the Secretary-General.
Closing remarks will be made by the Secretary-General.
The special event will be webcast live on the Internet at the following address: http://www.un.org/webcast/events/iyv.
Information and documentation can be obtained on the official Web site for the International Year (http://www.iyv2001.org).
For more information, please contact Ms. Yuko Osawa at United Nations Volunteers (tel.: (212) 906-3634).

There will be informal consultations to prepare negotiations on the consolidated text of the International Strategy for Action on Ageing (3-7 December 2001).
The next informal consultations will be held on Wednesday, 5 December, at 3 p.m. in Conference Room 1.
The resumed session of the Preparatory Committee for the Second World Assembly on Ageing will be held from 10 to 14 December 2001.
The consolidated text of the International Strategy may be viewed and downloaded on the Web site of the United Nations Programme on Ageing at the following address: (<http:// www.un.org/esa/socdev/ageing/waa/strategycons.doc>).
Copies of the text are also available outside of the office of Mr. John Langmore, Director, Division for Social Policy and Development, Department of Economic and Social Affairs (room DC2-1370).
The Bureau of the Commission on the Status of Women invites delegations to propose names for panellists to participate in the forty-sixth session of the Commission on the Status of Women (4-15 March 2002).
There will be two panels focusing on the following thematic issues being taken up by the Commission: (1) Eradicating poverty, including through the empowerment of women throughout their life cycle in a globalizing world; and (2) Environmental management and mitigation of natural disasters: a gender perspective.
Delegations are kindly requested to submit names and curricula vitae to the Division for the Advancement of Women (room DC2-1259), no later than Friday, 7 December 2001.

The second regular session of the UNICEF Executive Board will take place from 10 to 14 December 2001 in the Economic and Social Council Chamber.
The provisional annotated agenda and organization of work are contained in document E/ICEF/2001/12. ANNOUNCEMENTS

The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) and the World Trade Organization (WTO) are jointly organizing a workshop on international trade negotiations, as part of their International Trade Series.
The workshop, to be conducted in English, will be held from Monday to Thursday, 10 to 13 December 2001, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m. and 3 p.m. to 6 p.m. at United Nations Headquarters.
A letter on this subject, including a detailed information note, the programme and a nomination form, was addressed to all Permanent Missions in New York.
The registration deadline is Wednesday, 5 December.
For further information, please contact Ms. Cecelia Coleman at UNITAR (room DC1-603, tel.: 963-9684 and 963-9196).
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) is conducting a workshop on team development.
This workshop, to be conducted in English, will be held on Tuesday, 18 December 2001, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m. and from 3 p.m. to 6 p.m., and on Wednesday, 19 December, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m.
A letter on this subject, including a detailed information note, an outline of activities and a nomination form, was addressed to all Permanent Missions in New York.
Members from United Nations agencies are also encouraged to apply.
The registration deadline is Tuesday, 11 December.
For further information, please contact Ms. Cecelia Coleman at UNITAR (room DC1-603; tel.: (212) 963-9684 and 963-9196).
As from Monday, 3 December 2001, and for the rest of the month, the President of the Security Council will conduct informal briefings daily on the current work of the Council for Member States of the United Nations which are non-members of the Council, except on days on which no informal consultations are scheduled.
The briefings will take place immediately following the adjournment of the informal consultations in the Press Briefing Room (S-226).
A Web site of the Presidency of the Security Council has been established with effect on Thursday, 1 November 2001 and can be visited at the following address: <http://www.un.org/Docs/sc/presidency>.
The Web site of the President of the General Assembly can be visited at the following address: <http:// www. un.org/ga/president>.
The President's statements and a summary of his daily activities are available on this Web site.

Friday, 30 November 2001
THIRD COMMITTEE 53rd meeting
Advancement of women [112]
The Committee resumed its consideration of the item.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.22
The Committee was informed that the draft resolution contained no programme budget implications.
The representative of Australia orally revised the text and announced that Burkina Faso, India, Jamaica, Samoa, the Sudan, the United Republic of Tanzania and Vanuatu joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Subsequently, Bangladesh, Bulgaria, Cameroon, Colombia, Côte d'Ivoire, El Salvador, Eritrea, Ghana, Haiti, Honduras, Malaysia, Mauritania, Mauritius, Mozambique, Saint Lucia, Somalia, Togo, Trinidad and Tobago, Tunisia and Zambia joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, as orally revised, without a vote.
Implementation of the outcome of the Fourth World Conference on Women and of the twenty-third special session of the General Assembly entitled "Women 2000: gender equality, development and peace for the twenty-first century" [113]
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.80
The Vice-Chairman, Mr. Carlos Enrique García González (El Salvador) informed the Committee of the outcome of consultations on the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, without a vote.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of agenda item 113.
Human rights questions, including alternative approaches for improving the effective enjoyment of human rights and fundamental freedoms [119 (b)]
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.43/Rev.1
The Committee was informed that the revised draft resolution contained no programme budget implications.
The representative of South Africa (on behalf of the Non-Aligned Movement and China) made a statement.
Costa Rica, Mexico and Uruguay joined in sponsoring the revised draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the revised draft resolution, by a recorded vote of 116 to 3, with 42 abstentions.
Statements in explanation of vote before the vote were made by the representatives of Algeria, Canada (also on behalf of Australia and New Zealand) and Belgium (on behalf of the European Union).
The representative of the United States made a statement in explanation of vote after the vote.
Statements were made by the representatives of Egypt and Benin.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.64
A statement was made by the representative of Egypt.
Jordan, Lesotho, Mauritius and Somalia joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, by a recorded vote of 109 to 44, with 10 abstentions.
A statement in explanation of vote before the vote was made by the representative of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union).
Statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of Canada (also on behalf of Australia, New Zealand, Norway, Iceland and Liechtenstein), and the United States.
Statements were made by the representatives of Egypt, Benin, the Libyan Arab Jamahiriya and the Sudan.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.69/Rev.1 and programme budget implications contained in A/C.3/56/L.81
The Committee was informed that the programme budget implications contained in A/C.3/56/L.81 also pertained to A/C.3/56/L.69/Rev.1.
A statement was made by the representative of the Democratic Republic of the Congo.
Benin and Sierra Leone joined in sponsoring the revised draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the revised draft resolution, without a vote.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.71
The Secretary read out the revisions made to the text at the time of introduction of the draft resolution.
The representative of Mexico further revised the draft resolution.
Lesotho and Swaziland joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, as further orally revised, without a vote.
After the adoption of the draft resolution, statements were made by the representatives of Mexico, Bolivia and Singapore.
Human rights situations and reports of special rapporteurs and representatives [119 (c)]
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.50
The Chairman read out the oral revision that had been made to the text at the time of its introduction.
The representative of Belgium announced that Albania had joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Statements were made by the representatives of Yemen and the Islamic Republic of Iran, as well as by the representative of Suriname, who withdrew as a sponsor of the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, as orally revised, by a recorded vote of 71 to 53, with 41 abstentions.
Statements in explanation of vote before the vote were made by the representatives of the Libyan Arab Jamahiriya and China; statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of Chile, the Philippines, the Bahamas, Brazil and Suriname.
A statement was made by the representative of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines with regard to his vote.
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.58/Rev.1
Statements were made by the representatives of Belgium and the Sudan.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution by a recorded vote of 82 to 34, with 45 abstentions.
Statements in explanation of vote before the vote were made by the representatives of China, Egypt, the Libyan Arab Jamahiriya and Cuba; statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of Suriname and the Bahamas.
A statement was made by the representative of Canada.
A statement was made by the representative of the Sudan on a point of order.

55th meeting
Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.57

The representative of Belgium announced that Latvia had joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.

Action on draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.59
The representative of Algeria announced that Ecuador and Guatemala had joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Subsequently, El Salvador, the Democratic Republic of the Congo and Suriname joined in sponsoring the draft resolution.
Statements were made by the representatives of Egypt, Algeria, the Russian Federation, Turkey, India, Peru and Mauritania.
The Committee adopted the revised draft resolution, by a recorded vote of 84 to none, with 64 abstentions.
Statements in explanation of vote before the vote were made by the representatives of the United States, Chile, Canada, Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) and Argentina.
Statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of the Syrian Arab Republic, Liechtenstein and Japan.
A statement was made by the representative of Benin.

Programme budget implications of draft resolutions
The Committee had before it statements submitted by the Secretary-General on programme budget implications of draft resolutions contained in documents A/C.5/56/13, A/C.5/56/15, A/C.5/56/21, A/C.5/56/16 and A/C.5/56/18.
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions introduced the related report of that Committee (A/56/644) regarding document A/C.5/ 56/13 and orally introduced the other related reports of that Committee which were circulated, and requested that his statement be fully reflected in the summary records of the Fifth Committee.
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/C.1/56/L.47: Illicit trade in small arms and light weapons in all its aspects (A/C.5/56/13 and A/56/644)
Statements were made by the representatives of the United States, China, Canada, Cuba, Mexico and South Africa.
Following the general discussion on programme budget implications of draft resolution A/C.1/56/L.47, statements were made by the representatives of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union), Cuba, the Islamic Republic of Iran (on behalf of the Group of 77 and China), Canada, South Africa and China.
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions, the Director of the Programme Planning and Budget Division and the Chairman of the Committee also made statements.
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.6/Rev.1, as orally revised: Preparations for the substantive preparatory process and the Second World Assembly on Ageing (A/C.5/56/15)
Statements were made by the representatives of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union), the United States, Japan, Australia and Canada.
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.31: Use of mercenaries as a means of violating human rights and impeding the exercise of the right of peoples to self-determination (A/C.5/56/21)
No statements were made on this question.
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/C.3/56/L.26: Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women (A/C.5/56/16)
Statements were made by the representatives of the United States, India and Japan.
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/56/L.7: Special session of the General Assembly on children (A/C.5/56/18)
Statements were made by the representatives of the United States, China and Canada.
The representative of the Islamic Republic of Iran (on behalf of the Group of 77 and China) made a statement.
The Chairman also made a statement.

Special tribute to Mr. Ismat T. Kittani
There will be special tribute to the memory of Mr. Ismat T. Kittani, former President of the General Assembly, United Nations Under-Secretary-General and senior Iraqi diplomat, today, 4 December 2001, at 12 noon in the Economic and Social Council Chamber, with the participation of the Secretary-General.
All attending are kindly requested to be seated in the Chamber by 11.45 a.m.
International Volunteer Day
On Wednesday, 5 December 2001, International Volunteer Day, at 12 noon, immediately following the adjournment of the 76th plenary meeting of the General Assembly, an informal segment of the General Assembly marking the closing of the International Year of Volunteers 2001 (IYV), to be presided by the President of the General Assembly, will take place in the General Assembly Hall.
The event will be held in connection with the two plenary meetings of the General Assembly, which will be devoted to volunteering as decided by the General Assembly in its resolution 55/57.
Guest speakers will include His Royal Highness Prince of Asturias, D. Felipe de Borbon of Spain, and Dr. Nafis Sadik, former Executive Director of UNFPA, both appointed IYV Eminent Persons by the Secretary-General.
Closing remarks will be made by the Secretary-General.
The special event will be Webcast live at the following address: <http://www.un.org/webcast/events/ iyv>.
Information and documentation can be obtained on the official Web site for the International Year (<http://www.iyv 2001.org>).
For more in-formation, please contact Ms. Yuko Osawa at United Nations Volunteers (tel.: (212) 906-3634).
Human Rights Day
A forum on "The Media's Impact on Today's United Nations Anti-Discrimination Agenda" will take place on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 10.30 a.m. to 12 noon in Conference Room 4.
Shashi Tharoor, Interim Head of the Department of Public Information, will be the moderator of the forum.
The event is organized by the Department of Public Information, in cooperation with the Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights.
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of the non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.
For further information, please contact Ms. Laufey Love, Public Affairs Division, Department of Public Information (tel.: (212) 963-3507) or Mr. Oleg Dzioubinski, NGO Section, Department of Public Information (tel.: (212) 963-1859).
Special event
In support of the United Nations Year of Dialogue among Civilizations, the Department of Economic and Social Affairs, in collaboration with the International Council for Caring Communities (ICCC), will hold a special meeting on the theme "Music, Culture, Technology and Healthcare" on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 2.15 p.m. to 6 p.m. in Conference Room 4.
Mr. Sarbuland Khan, Director of the Division for ECOSOC Support and Coordination, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be among the participants.
Further information can be obtained at the following Inrernet address: <http://www.un.org/events/dec_6htm>.
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.
International Year of Mountains
The global launch of the International Year of Mountains 2002 will take place on Tuesday, 11 December 2001, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in Conference Room 2.
The former President of the Swiss Confederation, H.E. Mr. Adolf Ogi, will preside.
Welcoming remarks will be made by H.E. Mr. Murari Raj Sharma, Vice-President of the fifty-sixth session of the General Assembly.
Mr. Nitin Desai, Under-Secretary-General for Economic and Social Affairs, will make an address on behalf of the Secretary-General.
Mr. Jacques Diouf, Director-General, Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations, will deliver a keynote address on the International Year of Mountains.
Brief statements will be made by H.E. Mr. Kurmanbek Bakiev, Prime Minister of the Kyrgyz Republic, and Mr. Diego García Sayán, Minister for Foreign Affairs of Peru.
Mr. Nitin Desai will moderate a round table discussion, followed by a debate, on "Three Conditions for Sustainability in Mountain Development".
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.

SECOND COMMITTEE 36th meeting
Report of the Economic and Social Council [12]
Action on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.27
The Vice-Chairman of the Committee, Mr. Felix Mbayu (Cameroon), reported on the outcome of the informal consultations held on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.27 and orally amended the resolution.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, as orally amended.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of the item.
Macroeconomic policy questions [95]
(a) Trade and development
The Committee resumed its consideration of the item.
Action on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.36
The Committee was informed that the draft resolution contained no programme budget implications.
The Committee adopted the draft resolution, by a recorded vote of 74 to 1, with 47 abstentions.
The representative of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) made a statement in explanation of vote after the vote.
The following representatives made statements: Pakistan, Dominican Republic, Myanmar, Uganda, Bangladesh, Cape Verde, Viet Nam, Cambodia, Democratic People's Republic of Korea and Gabon.
(b) International financial system and development
Action on draft resolutions A/C.2/56/L.33 and A/C.56/ L.44
The Vice-Chairman of the Committee, Mr. Felix Mbayu (Cameroon), introduced draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.44, which he submitted on the basis of informal consultations held on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.33.
The representative of Belgium made a statement.
The Committee adopted draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.44, as orally corrected.
In light of the adoption of draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.44, draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.33 was withdrawn by its sponsors.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of agenda sub-item 95 (b).
(d) External debt crisis and development
Action on draft resolutions A/C.2/56/L.32 and A/C.2/56/ L.43
The Vice-Chairman of the Committee, Mr. Felix Mbayu (Cameroon), introduced draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.43, which he submitted on the basis of informal consultations held on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.32.
The Committee adopted draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.43.
In light of the adoption of draft resolution A/C.2/56/ L.43, draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.32 was withdrawn by its sponsors.

Permanent sovereignty of the Palestinian people in the Occupied Palestinian Territory, including Jerusalem, and of the Arab population in the occupied Syrian Golan over their natural resources [101]
Action on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.29
The Committee was informed that Djibouti should have been listed among the original co-sponsors of the draft resolution instead of Denmark.
The Committee was also in- formed that Senegal had subsequently joined in co-sponsoring the resolution.
The Vice-Chairman of the Committee, Mr. Dharmansjah Djumala (Indonesia), informed the Committee on the outcome of the informal consultations held on draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.29.
The Committee then proceeded to a recorded vote on the draft resolution.
A statement in explanation of vote before the vote was made by the representative of Israel.
The observer for Palestine made a statement.
Draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.29 was then adopted by a recorded vote of 131 to 3, with 2 abstentions.
Statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) and Japan.
The representatives of Mozambique, Uganda and Bangladesh stated that had they been present at the time of the vote, they would have voted in favour of the resolution.
Globalization and interdependence [105]

The Committee adopted draft resolution A/C.2/56/L.47.

International Volunteer Day
Today, 5 December 2001, International Volunteer Day, at 12 noon, immediately following the adjournment of the 75th plenary meeting of the General Assembly, an informal segment of the General Assembly marking the closing of the International Year of Volunteers 2001 (IYV), to be presided by the President of the General Assembly, will take place in the General Assembly Hall.
The event will be held in connection with the two plenary meetings of the General Assembly, which will be devoted to volunteering as decided by the General Assembly in its resolution 55/57.
Guest speakers will include His Royal Highness Prince of Asturias, D. Felipe de Borbon of Spain, and Dr. Nafis Sadik, former Executive Director of UNFPA, both appointed IYV Eminent Persons by the Secretary-General.
Closing remarks will be made by the Secretary-General.
The special event will be webcast live at the following address: <http://www.un.org/webcast/events/iyv>.
Information and documentation can be obtained on the official Web site for the International Year (<http://www.iyv2001. org>).
For more information, please contact Ms. Yuko Osawa at United Nations Volunteers (tel.: (212) 906-3634).
Human Rights Day
A forum on the media's impact on today's United Nations anti-discrimination agenda, entitled "News vs. Propaganda: The Gatekeepers' Dilemma" will take place on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 10.30 a.m. to 12 noon in Conference Room 4.
This event, held as part of the regular DPI/NGO briefing programme in observance of the Human Rights Day, will feature Mary Robinson, High Commissioner for Human Rights; Lakhdar Brahimi, Special Representative of the Secretary-General for Afghanistan; Hafez Al Mirazi, Washington Bureau Chief, Al Jazeera; Steve Williams, Senior Editor, BBC World News; Karen Curry, Vice-President and New York Bureau Chief, CNN; Mathatha Tsedu, Deputy Chief of News, South African Broadcasting Corporation; Abdel Bari Atwan, Editor-in-Chief, Al Quds Al-Arabi; and Barbara Crossette, Correspondent, New York Times.
Shashi Tharoor, Interim Head of the Department of Public Information, will be the moderator of the forum.
The event is organized by the Department of Public Information, in cooperation with the Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights.
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of the non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.
For further information, please contact Ms. Laufey Love, Public Affairs Division, Department of Public Information (tel.: (212) 963-3507) or Mr. Oleg Dzioubinski, NGO Section, Department of Public Information (tel.: (212) 963-1859).
Special event
In support of the United Nations Year of Dialogue among Civilizations, the Department of Economic and Social Affairs, in collaboration with the International Council for Caring Communities (ICCC), will hold a special meeting on the theme "Music, Culture, Technology and Healthcare" on Thursday, 6 December 2001, from 2.15 p.m. to 6 p.m. in Conference Room 4.
Mr. Sarbuland Khan, Director of the Division for ECOSOC Support and Coordination, Department of Economic and Social Affairs, will be among the participants.
Further information can be obtained at the following Inrernet address: <http://www.un.org/events/dec_6htm>.
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.
International Year of Mountains
The global launch of the International Year of Mountains 2002 will take place on Tuesday, 11 December 2001, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in Conference Room 2.
The former President of the Swiss Confederation, H.E. Mr. Adolf Ogi, will preside.
Welcoming remarks will be made by H.E. Mr. Murari Raj Sharma, Vice-President of the fifty-sixth session of the General Assembly.
Mr. Nitin Desai, Under-Secretary-General for Economic and Social Affairs, will make an address on behalf of the Secretary-General.
Mr. Jacques Diouf, Director-General, Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations, will deliver a keynote address on the International Year of Mountains.
Brief statements will be made by H.E. Mr. Kurmanbek Bakiev, Prime Minister of the Kyrgyz Republic, and Mr. Diego García Sayán, Minister for Foreign Affairs of Peru.
Mr. Nitin Desai will moderate a round table discussion, followed by a debate, on "Three Conditions for Sustainability in Mountain Development".
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend. Web sites

Open-ended informal consultations on the draft resolution on the safety and security of humanitarian personnel and protection of United Nations personnel, under agenda item 20, organized by the delegation of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union), will be held on Tuesday, 11 December 2001, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in the Trusteeship Council Chamber.
All delegations are invited to attend.
The Bureau of the Commission on the Status of Women invites delegations to propose names for panellists to participate in the forty-sixth session of the Commission on the Status of Women (4-15 March 2002).
There will be two panels focusing on the following thematic issues being taken up by the Commission: (1) Eradicating poverty, including through the empowerment of women throughout their life cycle in a globalizing world; and (2) Environmental management and mitigation of natural disasters: a gender perspective.
Delegations are kindly requested to submit names and curricula vitae to the Division for the Advancement of Women, by hand-delivery to room DC2-1260, by fax ((212)-963-3463); or by e-mail (daw@un.org), no later than Friday, 14 December 2001. ANNOUNCEMENTS

SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Friday, 7 December 2001
4435th (private) meeting
Meeting of the Security Council with Troop Contributing Countries to the United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus (UNFICYP) pursuant to resolution 1353 (2001), annex II, A
The Security Council met in private.
At the close of the meeting, the following communiqué was issued by the Secretary-General in accordance with rule 55 of the provisional rules of procedure of the Council:
"On 7 December 2001, the Security Council, pursuant to Annex II, Section A of resolution 1353 (2001), held its 4435th
meeting in private with the troop-contributing countries to the United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus (UNFICYP).
"The Security Council and the troop-contributing countries heard a briefing under rule 39 of its provisional rules of procedure by Mr. Joachim Hütter, Director of Europe and Latin America Division of the Department of Peacekeeping Operations.
"The members of the Council had a constructive exchange of views with representatives of participating troop-contributing countries."

The General Assembly continued its consideration of agenda item 21.
Statements were made by the representatives of Venezuela, Slovakia, the Russian Federation, Liechtenstein, Bangladesh and Pakistan.
The representative of the Netherlands made a statement in the course of which he introduced draft resolution A/56/L.30.
Statements were made by the representatives of Kenya, Namibia, Jamaica (on behalf of the Group of Latin American and Caribbean States), Mexico, Brazil, Chad, Latvia, Armenia and Dominica (on behalf of the Caribbean Community).
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 44/6 of 17 October 1989, the observer for the Council of Europe made a statement.
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 48/5 of 13 October 1993, the Secretary-General for the Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe made a statement.
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 477 (V) of 1 November 1950, the observer for the League of Arab States made a statement.
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 2011 (XX) of 11 October 1965, the observer for the Organization of African Unity made a statement.
Programme of work
The General Assembly was informed of the following additions to its programme of work: on Thursday, 13 December 2001, as the first item in the morning, the General Assembly will take up agenda item 14 (Report of the International Atomic Energy Agency) to consider draft resolution A/56/L.10 and the amendment thereto contained in document A/56/L.11; on the same morning, as the second item, the General Assembly will consider a number of draft resolutions under agenda item 20 (Strengthening of the coordination of humanitarian and disaster relief assistance of the United Nations, including special economic assistance) and its sub-items.
The Assembly was also informed that agenda item 37 (The role of diamonds in fuelling conflict), originally scheduled for the morning of Friday, 14 December 2001, was postponed to a later date.
80th plenary meeting
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 3369 (XXX) of 10 October 1975, the observer for the Organization of the Islamic Conference made a statement.
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 33/18 of 10 November 1978 and decision 53/453 of 18 December 1998, the observer for the International Organization of la Francophonie made a statement.
In accordance with General Assembly resolution 55/161 of 12 December 2000, the Deputy Secretary-General of the Economic Community of Central African States made a statement.
Statements in explanation of vote before the vote were made by the representatives of the United States, Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) and Australia.

The General Assembly adopted draft resolution A/56/L.26 (resolution 56/40).
The General Assembly adopted draft resolution A/56/L.29 (resolution 56/41).

International Year of Mountains
The global launch of the International Year of Mountains 2002 will take place on Tuesday, 11 December 2001, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in Conference Room 2.
The former President of the Swiss Confederation, H.E. Mr. Adolf Ogi, will preside.
Welcoming remarks will be made by H.E. Mr. Murari Raj Sharma, Vice-President of the fifty-sixth session of the General Assembly.
Mr. Nitin Desai, Under-Secretary-General for Economic and Social Affairs, will make an address on behalf of the Secretary-General.
Mr. Jacques Diouf, Director-General, Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations, will deliver a keynote address on the International Year of Mountains.
Brief statements will be made by H.E. Mr. Kurmanbek Bakiev, Prime Minister of the Kyrgyz Republic, H.E. Mr. Alan Wagner, Ambassador of Peru to the United States and former Minister for Foreign Relations; Mr. Alberto Gagliardi, Under-Secretary of State for Regional Affairs, Prime Minister's Office, Italy; and Mr. Josef Plank, Secretary for Agriculture, Niederosterreich, Austria; and Mr. Louis Besson, Member of Parliament and Mayor of Chambéry, France.
Mr. Nitin Desai will moderate a round table discussion, followed by a debate, on "Three Conditions for Sustainability in Mountain Development".
Members of permanent missions, Secretariat staff, representatives of non-governmental organizations and the media are invited to attend.

SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Friday, 14 December 2001
4436th meeting
The situation in Cyprus
Report of the Secretary-General on the United Nations operation in Cyprus (S/2001/1122)
The agenda was adopted without objection.
The President drew attention to the text of a draft resolution contained in document S/2001/1190, which had been prepared in the course of the Council's prior consultations.
The Council then proceeded to the vote on the draft resolution before it (S/2001/1190).
Decision: The draft resolution (S/2001/1190) received 15 votes in favour, none against and no abstentions, and was adopted unanimously as resolution 1384 (2001).
4437th meeting
The situation concerning the Democratic Republic of the Congo
Letter dated 10 November 2001 from the Secretary-General addressed to the President of the Security Council (S/2001/1072)
The President, with the consent of the Council, invited the representatives of Angola, Belgium, Burundi, Canada, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, Japan, Namibia, Nigeria, Rwanda, South Africa, Uganda, the United Republic of Tanzania, Zambia and Zimbabwe at their requests, to participate in the discussion of the item without the right to vote, in accordance with the relevant provisions of the Charter and rule 37 of the Council's provisional rules of procedure.
In the absence of objection, the President, with the consent of the Council, extended an invitation under rule 39 of the Council's provisional rules of procedure to Mr. Mahmoud Kassem, Chairman of the Expert Panel on the Illegal Exploitation of Natural Resources and Other Forms of Wealth in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.
The Council began its consideration of the item.
The Council heard a statement under rule 39 of its provisional rules of procedure by Mr. Mahmoud Kassem.
The Council heard a statement by the Minister for Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation of the Democratic Republic of the Congo, His Excellency Mr. Leonard She Okitundu, the Third Deputy Prime Minister and Minister for Foreign Affairs of Uganda, His Excellency Mr. James Wapakabulo, the Deputy Minister for Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation of the United Republic of Tanzania, His Excellency Mr Abdulkadeer Shareef, and the Adviser to the President of Rwanda, His Excellency Mr. Patrick Mazimhaka.
Statements were made by the representatives of France, Norway, Ireland, Jamaica, Bangladesh, Mauritius, Ukraine, the United Kingdom, the United States, the Russian Federation, Singapore, Tunisia, Colombia, China, and by the President, speaking in his capacity as the representative of Mali.
The Council then heard a statement by the Minister for Foreign Affairs of Zimbabwe, His Excellency Mr. I.S.G. Mudenge.
The meeting was suspended.
Upon resumption of the meeting, statements were made by the representatives of South Africa, Canada, Belgium (speaking on behalf of the European Union and the Central and Eastern Europe associated with the European Union - Bulgaria, Estonia, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, the Czech Republic, Poland, Romania, Slovakia and Slovenia - and the associated countries of Cyprus, Malta and Turkey and Liechtenstein, EFTA country belonging to the European Economic Area, which aligned themselves with the statement), Angola, Burundi, Nigeria, Zambia, Namibia and Japan.
Mr. Mahmoud Kassem responded to comments and questions posed by members of the Council.
4438th meeting
The situation in the Middle East, including the Palestinian Question
Letter dated 13 December 2001 from the Permanent Representative of Egypt to the United Nations addressed to the President of the Security Council (S/2001/1191)
The President, with the consent of the Council, invited the representatives of Belgium, Brazil, Canada, Cuba, Egypt, the Islamic Republic of Iran, Israel, Malaysia and South Africa, at their requests, to participate in the discussion of the item without the right to vote, in accordance with the relevant provisions of the Charter and rule 37 of the Council's provisional rules of procedure.
The President drew attention to a letter dated 14 December 2001 from the Permanent Observer of Palestine to the United Nations (S/2001/1205), requesting an invitation to participate in the meeting in accordance with the Council's previous practice.
In accordance with the rules of procedure and the previous practice in this regard, the President, with the consent of the Council, invited the Permanent Observer of Palestine to the United Nations to participate in the discussion.
In response to the request contained in a letter dated 14 December 2001 from the Chairman of the Committee on the Exercise of the Inalienable Rights of the Palestinian People, the President extended an invitation under rule 39 of the Council's provisional rules of procedure to the Chairman of the Committee on the Exercise of the Inalienable Rights of the Palestinian People, Mr. Papa Louis Fall.
The President drew attention to the text of a draft resolution contained in document S/2001/1199, submitted by Egypt and Tunisia.
The Council began its consideration of the item and heard a statement by the Permanent Observer of Palestine.
Statements were made by the representatives of Tunisia, Egypt, Mauritius, the United Kingdom, Ukraine, the United States, Jamaica, Singapore, the Russian Federation, China, Colombia, Bangladesh, Norway, South Africa and Israel.
In accordance with the decision taken earlier at the meeting, the Council heard a statement under rule 39 of its provisional rules of procedure by Mr. Papa Louis Fall.
Statements were made by the representatives of Cuba, Malaysia, Canada, Brazil, the Islamic Republic of Iran and Belgium, (speaking on behalf of the European Union and the Central and Eastern Europe associated with the European Union - Bulgaria, Estonia, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, the Czech Republic, Poland, Romania, Slovakia and Slovenia - and the associated countries of Cyprus, Malta and Turkey and Liechtenstein, EFTA country belonging to the European Economic Area, which aligned themselves with the statement).
Before the vote, statements were made by the representatives of France and Ireland, and by the President, speaking in his capacity as the representative of Mali.
The Council then proceeded to the vote on the draft resolution (S/2001/1199) before it.
Decision: The draft resolution (S/2001/1199) received 12 votes in favour, one against (the United States of America), 2 abstentions (Norway and the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland), and was not adopted, owing to the negative vote of a permanent member of the Council.

SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Thursday, 20 December 2001
4443rd meeting
The situation in Afghanistan
The agenda was adopted without objection.
The President, with the consent of the Council, invited the representative of Afghanistan, at his request, to participate in the discussion of the item without the right to vote, in accordance with the relevant provisions of the Charter and rule 37 of the Council's provisional rules of procedure.
The President drew attention to the text of a draft resolution contained in document S/2001/1228, which had been prepared in the course of the Council's prior consultations, and made an oral revision to the text in its provisional form.
The Council proceeded to the vote on the draft resolution before it (S/2001/1228), as orally revised in its provisional form.
Decision: The draft resolution (S/2001/1228), as orally revised in its provisional form, received 15 votes in favour, none against, and no abstentions, and was adopted unanimously as resolution 1386 (2001).
89th plenary meeting
(a) Reports of the Secretary-General (A/56/681, A/56/687)
(b) Draft resolution (A/56/L.62)
The representative of Germany made statement in the course of which he introduced draft resolution A/56/L.62.
Statements were made by the representatives of Afghanistan, Belgium (on behalf of the European Union and Bulgaria, Cyprus, the Czech Republic, Estonia, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, Malta, Poland, Romania, Slovakia, Slovenia and Turkey), the Republic of Korea, Norway, the Islamic Republic of Iran, Pakistan, Japan, India, the United States, Ukraine, Turkey, Colombia, Bangladesh, Canada, Nepal and Uzbekistan.
The President informed the General Assembly that in order to allow time to the Fifth Committee to review the programme budget implications of draft resolution A/56/L.62, action on the draft resolution was postponed.
Tenth emergency special session
15th plenary meeting
Resumption of the tenth emergency special session
The President of the General Assembly declared resumed the tenth emergency special session of the General Assembly pursuant to Assembly resolution ES-10/7 of 20 October 2000.
The President drew the attention of delegations to documents A/ES-10/130 and A/ES-10/131.
The President informed members that, in accordance with rule 63 of the rules of procedures of the General Assembly, the President and the Vice-Presidents of the fifty-sixth session would serve in the same capacity as the resumed tenth emergency session.
On the proposal of the President, the General Assembly decided that the Credential Committee at the resumed tenth emergency special session would consist of the same members as those appointed at the fifty-sixth session.
The General Assembly took note of a letter by the Secretary-General (A/ES-10/132) concerning 14 Member States that were in arrears in the payment of their financial contribution to the United Nations within the term of Article 19 of the Charter.
Illegal Israeli actions in Occupied East Jerusalem and the rest of the Occupied Palestinian Territory: draft resolutions (A/ES-10/L.7 (A/ES-10/L.7A), A/ES-10/L.8 (A/ES-10/L.7B)) [5]
The President made a technical correction to document A/ES-10/L.7 to the effect that the sponsors had submitted two separate draft resolutions and that the two draft resolutions had been issued as Part A and Part B of document A/ES-10/L.7.
In accordance with the intention of the sponsors, Part A should have been issued as document A/ES-10/L.7 and Part B should have been issued as document A/ES-10/L.8.
Accordingly, the General Assembly considered two draft resolutions, A/ES-10/L.7 and A/ES-10/L.8.
The Assembly decided to waive the relevant provision of rule 78 of the rules of procedures and decided to consider draft resolutions A/ES-10/L.7 and A/ES-10/L.8.
The President made a statement.
The representative of Egypt (on behalf of the League of Arab States) made a statement in the course of which he introduced draft resolutions A/ES-10/L.7 and A/ES-10/L.8.
The observer of Palestine made a statement.
Statements were made by the representatives of South Africa (on behalf of the Non-Aligned Movement), Senegal (Chair-man of the Committee on the Exercise of the Inalienable Rights of the Palestinian People), Chile (on behalf of the Rio Group), the United Republic of Tanzania, the Islamic Republic of Iran, Israel, Qatar (on behalf of the Organization of the Islamic Conference), Norway, Cuba, the United States, the Russian Federation, Belgium (on behalf of the European Union and Bulgaria, Cyprus, the Czech Republic, Estonia, Hungary, Iceland, Latvia, Liechtenstein, Lithuania, Malta, Poland, Romania, Slovakia, Slovenia and Turkey), Canada, China, Japan, Maldives, Brazil and Bangladesh.
In accordance with the decision taken by the General Assembly at its 10th plenary meeting on 5 February 1999, the observer of Switzerland made a statement.
The representative of Turkey made a statement in explanation of vote before the vote.
By 124 votes to 6, with 25 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted draft resolution A/ES-10/L.7 (resolution ES-10/8).
By 133 votes to 4, with 16 abstentions (recorded vote), the General Assembly adopted draft resolution A/ES-10/L.8 (resolution ES-10/9).
Statements in explanation of vote after the vote were made by the representatives of Australia, Pakistan and Paraguay.
The General Assembly thus adjourned its tenth emergency special session in accordance with the terms of paragraph 3 of resolution ES-10/9.
FIFTH COMMITTEE 39th meeting
Note: The summary of the 39th meeting of the Fifth Committee will appear in the next issue of the Journal (No. 2001/248).
Resumed substantive session of 2001
46th meeting
Adoption of the agenda and other organizational matters [1]
The Council waived rule 20 of the rules of procedure of the Economic and Social Council.
Change of date for the organizational session of the Economic and Social Council, 2002
Oral decision
Upon the proposal of the President, the Council decided to set the date of its organizational session for 2002 to 12 to 15 February 2002.
Elections
Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues
In accordance with its resolution 2000/22 and decision 2001/316, the Council elected the following members by acclamation to the newly established Forum for a three-year term beginning on 1 January 2002: Njuma Ekudanayo (Democratic Republic of the Congo), Yuji Iwasawa (Japan) and Yuri Alexandrovitch Boitchenko (Russian Federation).
The Council proceeded to elect by secret ballot two members from Latin American and Caribbean States and two members from Western European and other States for a three-year term beginning on 1 January 2002.
Bettina Cadenbach (Germany) and Hans Plut (Austria) served as tellers.
The results of the secret ballot were as follows:
Latin American and Caribbean States: Votes
Otilia Lux García de Coti (Guatemala) 39
Marcos Matías Alonso (Mexico) 30
Ronald Karwofodi (Suriname) 19
María Fernanda Espinosa (Ecuador) 16
Having obtained the required majority, Otilia Lux García de Coti (Guatemala) and Marcos Matías Alonso (Mexico) were declared elected.
Western European and other States:
Wayne Lord (Canada) 49
Ida Nicolaisen (Denmark) 36
María Noguerol Álvarez (Spain) 20
Having obtained the required majority, Wayne Lord (Canada) and Ida Nicolaisen (Denmark) were declared elected.
Following a statement by the representative of the Russian Federation, the President of the Council read out the names of the eight members appointed by him to the Forum for a three-year term beginning on 1 January 2002: Antonio Jacanamijoy (Colombia), Ayitegau Kouevi (Togo), Willie Littlechild (Canada), Ole Henrik Magga (Norway), Zinaida Strogalschikova (Russian Federation), Parshuram Tamang (Nepal), Mililani Trask (United States of America) and Fortunato Turpo Choquehuanca (Peru).
The Council postponed to a future session the election of one member from Asian States for a three-year term beginning on 1 January 2002.
Statements were made by the representatives of the Sudan and Suriname.
Commission on Narcotic Drugs
The Council elected South Africa to fill a postponed vacancy on the Commission for a four-year term beginning on 1 January 2002.
Committee on Science and Technology for Development
The Council elected the Philippines to fill a postponed vacancy on the Commission for a term beginning on the date of election and expiring on 31 December 2004.
The Council postponed to a future session the election of one member from Asian States and one member from Western European and other States for a term beginning on the date of election and expiring on 31 December 2004.
Executive Board of the World Food Programme
The Council elected Australia and the United Kingdom to fill postponed vacancies on the Executive Board for a three-year term beginning on 1 January 2002.
Executive Board of the United Nations Children's Fund
The Council was informed that Bolivia would be unable to complete its term of office on the Board as of 1 January 2002.
The Council therefore elected Trinidad and Tobago to replace Bolivia from 1 January to 31 December 2002.

The representatives of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) and Syrian Arab Republic made statements regarding the French and Arabic language translations.
The Council thus concluded its consideration of sub-item (k).
(m) International cooperation on tax matters
The Council was informed that due to some technical issues the item could not be taken up at this session.
On the proposal of the President (Cameroon), the Council decided to defer the consideration of the report on the international cooperation on tax matters to the substantive session of the Economic and Social Council 2002.
Social and human rights questions [14]
(a) Advancement of women

Draft resolutions I and II (Part II)
The Council recommended the draft resolutions for adoption by the General Assembly and thus concluded its consideration of the recommendations contained in the revised report of the Commission.
The Council concluded its consideration of agenda item 14 as a whole.
Closure of the substantive session
The President made an statement.

The provisional annotated agenda and organization of work will be issued as document A/AC.257/31.
Delegations are requested to submit the names of their representatives to the Secretary of the Preparatory Committee, Ms. Vivian Pliner-Josephs (room S-2950E; fax: (212) 963-5935).

Workshop
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) and the United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs (DESA) are jointly conducting a Workshop on the priority theme of the fortieth session of the Commission for Social Development: Integration of social and economic policy.

Friday, 21 December 2001
SECURITY COUNCIL
4444th meeting
The situation in Angola
The agenda was adopted without objection.
In accordance with the understanding reached in the Council's prior consultations, the President, with the consent of the Council, extended an invitation under rule 39 of its provisional rules of procedure to Mr. Ibrahim Gambari, Under-Secretary-General, Special Adviser on Africa.
The Council began its consideration of the item and heard a statement under rule 39 of its provisional rules of procedure by Mr. Ibrahim Gambari.
Statements were then made by the representatives of Bangladesh, Jamaica, Norway, Ukraine, China, the United Kingdom, France, Ireland, Singapore, Colombia, the Russian Federation, Tunisia, Mauritius and the United States, and by the President, speaking in his capacity as the representative of Mali.
Mr. Gambari responded to comments made and questions posed.
Expression of condolences in connection with the death of His Excellency Mr. Léopold Sédar Senghor, former President of Senegal
The President made a statement on behalf of the Council.
The Council observed a minute of silence in tribute to the memory of His Excellency Mr. Léopold Sédar Senghor, former President of Senegal.
4445th meeting
Wrap up discussion on the work of the Security Council for the current month
The Council began its consideration of the item and heard an introductory statement by the President.
Statements were made by the representatives of Bangladesh, Tunisia, Ukraine, Jamaica, Norway, Colombia, the United Kingdom, China, the United States, Mauritius, Ireland, France, the Russian Federation and Singapore, and by the President, speaking in his capacity as the representative of Mali.

Delegations are kindly requested to submit the names of their representatives to the Secretary of the Commission, Ms. Vivian Pliner-Josephs (room S-2950E; fax: (212) 963-5935).
United Nations Children's Fund
EXECUTIVE BOARD
Pre-session briefing
An informal pre-session information briefing on major issues before the UNICEF Executive Board at its first regular session (21-25 January 2002) will take place on Thursday, 10 January 2002, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in the Economic and So-cial Council Chamber.
The provisional annotated agenda and organization of work are contained in document E/ICEF/2002/ 2.
All delegations are invited to attend.
First regular session for 2002
The first regular session of the UNICEF Executive Board will take place from 21 to 25 January 2002 in Conference Room 2.
The provisional annotated agenda and organization of work are contained in document E/ICEF/2002/2.
Delegations are requested to fax their credentials to the secretariat of UNICEF (fax: (212) 326-7096) as soon as possible, but no later than Monday, 7 January 2002.
In accordance with rule 50 (2) of the rules of procedure and its annex, observer delegations are also requested to communicate, with their credentials, their special interest in the items of the provisional agenda on which they intend to intervene.
Programme and of the United Nations Population Fund
Pre-session informal consultations
The Executive Board of UNDP and of UNFPA will hold pre-session informal consultations on all matters before the first regular session for 2002 on Friday, 11 January 2002, from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. in the Economic and Social Council Chamber.
The first regular session for 2002 of the Executive Board of UNDP and of UNFPA will be held from Monday, 28 January, to Friday, 8 February 2002, in Conference Room 2.
The joint session of the Executive Boards of UNDP/UNFPA and of UNICEF, with the participation of WFP, will take place on Monday, 28 January, from 3 p.m. to 6 p.m. in Conference Room 2.
The provisional agenda, annotations, list of documents and work plan are contained in document DP/2002/L.1.
Interested delegations are invited to attend.
Delegations, as well as observers, are requested to fax their credentials to the secretariat of the Executive Board (fax: (212) 906-5634) as soon as possible, but no later than Monday, 21 January 2002. ANNOUNCEMENTS
Copies of the information are available at the Department of Disarmament Affairs with Mr. Nazir Kamal (room S-3170F; tel.: (212) 963-6195), as well as with the Chairperson, Ms. Gabriela Martinic, Permanent Mission of Argentina (tel.: (212) 688-6300, extensions 226 and 224).
The Chairperson would also like to remind all delegations that they might submit further information.
Background information on the Secretary-General's report on the priority theme "Integration of social and economic policy" of the fortieth session of the Commission for Social Development (12-22 February 2002), is available to be picked up at the office of the Director of the Division for Social Policy and Development (room DC2-1370). It can also be downloaded from the Web site of the Division at: <www.un.org/ esa/socdev/csd/2002/htm>.
Workshop
The United Nations Institute for Training and Research (UNITAR) and the United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs (DESA) are jointly conducting a Workshop on the priority theme of the fortieth session of the Commission for Social Development: Integration of social and economic policy.
This workshop, to be conducted in English, will be held on Wednesday, 16 January 2002, from 9.45 a.m. to 1 p.m. and from 3 p.m. to 4.45 p.m.
A letter on this subject, including a detailed information note, the draft programme and a nomination form, was addressed to all Permanent Missions in New York.
The registration deadline is Wednesday, 9 January .
For further information, please contact Ms. Cecelia Coleman at UNITAR (room DC1-603, tel.: (212) 963- 9684 or (212) 963- 9196).
As from Monday, 3 December 2001, and for the rest of the month, the President of the Security Council will conduct informal briefings daily on the current work of the Council for Member States of the United Nations which are non-members of the Council, except on days on which no informal consultations are scheduled.
The briefings will take place immediately following the adjournment of the informal consultations in the Press Briefing Room (S-226).
Recorded information about previously unscheduled meetings and consultations of the whole of the Security Council may be obtained by calling (212) 963-8530.
Delegations who wish to make their statements available to the media at Headquarters are advised to provide 100 copies of these directly to the media office located on the third floor in the Secretariat Building (room S-348).
SUMMARY OF MEETINGS
Thursday, 20 December 2001
Fifty-sixth session
FIFTH COMMITTEE 39th meeting
Review of the efficiency of the administrative and financial functioning of the United Nations [121]
The Committee resumed its consideration of this agenda item.
Report of the Office of Internal Oversight Services on the audit of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees in Albania
The representative of Botswana, coordinator of informal consultations on this question, introduced draft decision A/C.5/56/L.27.
The Committee adopted, without a vote, the draft decision.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of this question.
Scale of assessments for the apportionment of the expenses of the United Nations [125]
The representative of India, coordinator of informal consultations on this agenda item, introduced draft resolution A/C.5/56/L.23 and made a statement regarding the understanding of the Committee in connection with paragraph 6 of the draft resolution.
The Committee adopted, without a vote, the draft resolution.
The representative of Cuba made a statement in explanation of position.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of this agenda item at this stage.
United Nations common system [127]
The Committee had before it draft resolution A/C.5/56/ L.15, submitted by the Chairman, which had been coordinated by the representative of Pakistan.
The representative of Belgium (on behalf of the European Union) made a statement.
The Committee thus concluded its consideration of this agenda item.
Financing of the International Tribunal for the Prosecution of Persons Responsible for Serious Violations of International Humanitarian Law Committed in the Territory of the Former Yugoslavia since 1991 [131]
The representative of Norway, coordinator of informal consultations on this item, introduced and orally revised draft resolution A/C.5/56/L.25.
The representative of India orally proposed an amendment to operative paragraph 8 of the draft resolution.
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions made a statement.
The representative of the Russian Federation also made a statement.
The Committee adopted, without a vote, the draft resolution, as orally revised and amended.
Financing of the International Criminal Tribunal for the Prosecution of Persons Responsible for Genocide and Other Serious Violations of International Humanitarian Law Committed in the Territory of Rwanda and Rwandan Citizens Responsible for Genocide and Other Such Violations Committed in the Territory of Neighbouring States between 1 January and 31 December 1994 [132]
The representative of Norway, coordinator of informal consultations on this item, introduced and orally revised draft resolution A/C.5/56/L.26.
The Committee adopted, without a vote, the draft resolution, as orally revised.
Proposed programme budget for the biennium 2002-2003 [123]
Programme budget implications of draft resolution A/56/L.62: Emergency international assistance for peace, normalcy and reconstruction of war-stricken Afghanistan and the situation in Afghanistan and its implications for international peace and security
The Director of the Programme Planning and Budget Division introduced the report of the Secretary-General (A/C.5/ 56/31).
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions introduced the related report of that Committee (A/56/720).
On the proposal of the Chairman, the Committee decided, without a vote, to inform the General Assembly that should it adopt draft resolution A/56/L.62, an amount of $7,355,400 would be charged against the provision of $93.7 million for special political missions requested under section 3, Political affairs, of the programme budget for the biennium 2002-2003.
Estimates in respect of matters of which the Security Council is seized (A/C.5/56/25/Add.1 and A/56/7/Add.6)
The Director of the Programme Planning and Budget Division introduced the report of the Secretary-General (A/C.5/ 56/25/Add.1).
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions introduced the related report of that Committee (A/56/7/Add.6).
Estimates in respect of matters of which the Security Council is seized (A/C.5/56/25/Add.2 and A/56/7/Add.7)
The Director of the Programme Planning and Budget Division introduced the report of the Secretary-General (A/C.5/ 56/25/Add.2).
The Chairman of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions introduced the related report of that Committee (A/56/7/Add.7).
On the proposal of the Chairman, the Committee decided, without a vote, to recommend to the General Assembly that it take note of the report of the Secretary-General contained in document A/C.5/56/25/Add.2 on the estimates in respect of matters of which the Security Council is seized; concur with the observations and recommendations of the Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions contained in paragraph 7 of its report and approve the charge of $1,413, 400 for the period from 1 January to 31 December 2002 for the Special Adviser of the Secretary-General for Cyprus (A/C.5/56/25/Add.2) against the provision for special political missions requested under section 3, Political affairs, of the proposed programme budget for the biennium 2002-2003.
